Powerful Overseas Chinese Figures 182

Preparing for the Overseas Chinese Association

Chen Wulie Sends Letters to Overseas Chinese in Various Ports

Overseas Chinese are the most important people in the history of the Republic of China. In short, they are the elements that created the Republic of China. Therefore, Mr. Sun Yat-sen especially praised overseas Chinese as the mother of the revolution, which is worthy of the name. Most of the strength of the revolutionary army was funded by overseas Chinese. Overseas Chinese cannot bear the harsh treatment of foreign races and are subjected to spiritual stimulation. They are determined to strengthen themselves and hope for the invigoration of the motherland. They do not hesitate to give up their homes and donate money to help the revolutionary army. However, after the revolutionary army succeeded, it was not able to redress even the slightest shame for overseas Chinese and devise a plan for their protection. This is what overseas Chinese are most disappointed and saddened by. Recently, in the case of the expulsion of Chinese from Mexico, overseas Chinese suffered losses of tens of millions, were displaced, and were in a miserable situation. The government was unable to maintain order, and the so-called benefactors and philanthropists in the country did not care. As a result, the tens of thousands of overseas Chinese in Mexico who had sacrificed for the party and the country were left to be slaughtered and were deported back to the country in batches. This is also the most unfortunate thing for overseas Chinese. However, there are also reasons for the adverse environment faced by overseas Chinese and their failure to achieve their goals in the motherland. The reason is that there is no truly linked and mutually supportive organization to provide effective support in the motherland. Moreover, during times of national crisis, overseas Chinese need such an organization even more to be the main driving force for self-salvation and national salvation. The most important place in the motherland is Shanghai. Shanghai is the center of economics and politics in the Far East and the area where overseas Chinese enter and leave the most. It is appropriate for both people and location to establish an overseas Chinese liaison organization here. Therefore, some powerful overseas Chinese figures in Shanghai, seeing this, have launched the Overseas Chinese Association. The details of the process have been recorded in previous newspapers, and its main figures are Zheng Hongnian, Tang Haian, Guo Shun, Wu Chengyu, and others from the political, business, and academic circles of overseas Chinese. Its content and organization are very strict and orderly, and it is a model for organizing social groups at sea. The process of its operation is recorded below in detail. The organization of the Overseas Chinese Association is divided into three stages: (1) The temporary preparatory period, which is dedicated to soliciting founders (hoping to reach 1,000 people) to strengthen its basic strength. (2) The preparatory period, actively promoting and launching a large-scale membership recruitment campaign in order to expand its own scope. (3) The establishment period, carrying out practical work to save the country and protect overseas Chinese, the first step is to make Shanghai a model area for saving the country, and the second step is to find ways to relieve the distressed or unemployed overseas Chinese in general, in order to realize its means of saving the country and protecting overseas Chinese and to complete an organization that truly struggles for the interests of overseas Chinese, in order to win the sympathy of the majority of overseas Chinese. If this plan can be carried out one by one, the reputation of the Overseas Chinese Association will not only be admired by overseas Chinese overseas, but also respected by the Chinese people. We sincerely hope that the founders of the association will work hard to achieve it. It is now heard that Mr. Chen Wulie, a giant in the Nanyang overseas Chinese community who recently returned to China, has also been aroused by the organization of the Overseas Chinese Association. To seek happiness for overseas Chinese and not let others do it, he has volunteered to organize a powerful overseas Chinese organization in Shanghai in order to realize his long-cherished wish to protect overseas Chinese, which shows that the establishment of an overseas Chinese organization in Shanghai is attracting the attention of overseas Chinese from all parties. Mr. Chen is currently residing at No. 70 Rue Amiral d'Estaing in the French Concession. The circular he is preparing to send to various ports is recorded below for quick viewing. The original letter reads: "Dear Sirs, In recent years, our country has been unfortunate, with internal and external troubles following one after another. The drought in Shaanxi and Gansu the year before last, the floods in Anhui and Hubei last year, and the loss of the Eastern Provinces on September 18 and the battle of Shanghai on January 28, our overseas Chinese compatriots have always rushed to the front, vying to donate. The government only sent a commissioner to comfort them and never took into account the interests of the overseas Chinese themselves. If the huge sums of money donated each time were used for public purposes, it would be pleasing to everyone. However, the money is sent to different people, and there is no organization in the country to supervise its use. As a result, the funds earned by the sweat of the overseas Chinese are wasted in vain, which is by no means a small amount. This is what Wulie has recently heard and learned since returning to China, and it is something that our overseas Chinese compatriots never dreamed of. Now that the country is in trouble, it depends on the efforts of the people at home and abroad to save it. However, we cannot give up eating because of choking. The only way to remedy the situation is to quickly establish a powerful overseas Chinese organization in Shanghai to serve as our eyes and ears. In this way, there will be no fear that future remittances to the country will be seized by unscrupulous people. Moreover, at a time when the world is facing financial panic and the collapse of production, it is especially important to seek a retreat in the country for the sake of the future of overseas Chinese so that the unemployed can avoid becoming refugees. However, this matter is too important to be accomplished without the joint efforts of everyone. Wulie will first go to Beijing and Wuhan in the next few days to visit the authorities and request that the power of the two provinces of Fujian and Guangdong in terms of construction be entrusted to our impartial overseas Chinese who return to the country to take office so that the country's resources can be gradually developed, so that there is no wasteland and the people are not idle, and then there will be no bandits, and the local area can achieve good governance. At the same time, we should request the National Government to instruct the competent authorities to instruct various railway bureaus and merchants to purchase wood, grain, and other local products operated by our overseas Chinese from Nanyang in order to save the fate of overseas Chinese merchants. If the government cares about overseas Chinese affairs, it will definitely adopt these relief measures. The results will be reported later. This matter concerns the interests of all overseas Chinese compatriots. If you agree, please reply immediately and send representatives to Shanghai to jointly prepare for the establishment of an organization. In particular, we hope that you will directly send a telegram to the Central National Government expressing your consistent position on the issue of requesting the provincial government's power in order to achieve the ultimate goal. We look forward to it. Sincerely, Mr. So-and-so, etc."

Thirty-three Years Since Last Appearance

Leo Meteor Shower

Announced by the Astronomical Observatory Research Institute

Around the 16th of this month

Meteors will fall like rain, resembling fireworks.

A "meteor shower" is a group of meteors appearing in space, radiating from a certain point in the sky and scattering in all directions. The activity of meteor showers has a predictable cycle. When they reach their peak, they fall densely like rain, what the ancients called "stars falling like rain," resembling the spectacle of fireworks and being extremely beautiful. There are countless meteor showers, but the Leo meteor shower is the most famous. It can be seen every year in mid-November, and its peak period cycles approximately every thirty-three years. Years such as 1833, 1866, and 1899 were all active periods. This year is 1932, thirty-three years since 1899. According to previous patterns, it is again approaching its peak. The period for the Leo meteor shower this year will be around November 13th or 14th at the earliest, and no later than the 18th or 19th. It is expected to be at its most intense on the 15th, 16th, and 17th. The location of Leo in the celestial sphere is approximately at right ascension 10 hours and declination north 23 degrees (this position, using old Chinese star names, is "Xuanyuan"). In mid-November, it appears in the east around 1 AM. By dawn, this constellation will have moved to the south. Therefore, observers should look east around 1 or 2 AM each night around the 16th, and shift their gaze to the southeast around 3 or 4 AM, ceasing observation around 4 or 5 AM to witness this spectacle.

For information on various aspects of the Leo meteor shower, please refer to the Chinese Astronomical Society's "Cosmos Monthly," Volume 2, Number 10. "Cosmos Monthly" is available for sale at the Zhengzhong Bookstore on Taiping Road in Nanjing and the Astronomical Exhibition Hall on Paozihe in Dongcheng, Beiping.

They arrived to greet him, and after the ship docked at the Kowloon Wharf, representatives from over eighty organizations boarded. After arriving in Hong Kong, Mr. Weng rested briefly on the seventh floor of the Gloucester Hotel before attending various banquets. His entourage included Luo Yinpu, Lin Junneng, and Chen Ding. Their journey would first take them to the Philippines, then the South Sea Islands, and finally to Europe and America.

Malaya Restricts Import Taxes on Chinese Goods 186

Revised Twice This Year

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce reported yesterday that, according to the special envoy of the China Chemical Industry Society's Nanyang inspection, Malaya, where many of our overseas Chinese reside, is a major market for our country's exports. Currently, the Malay Federation imposes heavy taxes on the import of Chinese goods, having revised them twice this year, which has severely impacted the transportation and sales of domestic products in Nanyang. A new tax rate list is attached, hoping that domestic goods manufacturers will pay attention. The key points of the tax rate are as follows: (A) Alcoholic Beverages 1) Chinese wine (including medicinal wine): 12 yuan per gallon; 2) Bitter wine and sour wine, with an alcohol content of no more than 100 percent: 13 yuan per gallon; 3) All kinds of sparkling wine, with an alcohol content of no more than 42 percent: 6 yuan per gallon. If it is British goods, it is only 5.5 yuan; 4) All kinds of non-sparkling wine (including medicinal wine), with an alcohol content of more than 20 percent but no more than 42 percent: 4.5 yuan per gallon. If it is British goods, it is 4.2 yuan; 5) All kinds of non-sparkling wine (including medicinal wine), with an alcohol content of no more than 26 percent: 1.5 yuan per gallon. If it is British goods, it is only 1.5 yuan; 6) Lager beer, stout, blood tonic stout, pear wine: 1.3 yuan per gallon. If it is British goods, it is only 1.2 yuan. (B) Tobacco Products 1) Cigars, also known as Luzon cigars and snuff: 1.6 yuan per pound; 2) Cigarettes: 1.1 yuan per pound. British goods are only 1 yuan; 3) Raw tobacco leaves: 0.7 yuan per pound; 4) Manufactured tobacco (excluding cigarettes and Luzon snuff), sealed in iron cans for import and sale (such as tobacco cakes): 1.1 yuan per pound. British goods are only 1 yuan. If not tightly sealed: 0.8 yuan per pound. White sugar, yellow sugar, brown sugar, rock sugar, coconut sugar, sugar cane, etc.: 0.03 yuan per pound. (D) Matches 1) Each box containing no more than ten matches: 0.12 yuan per hundred boxes; 2) Each box containing more than ten but no more than twenty matches: 0.24 yuan per hundred boxes; 3) Each box containing more than twenty but no more than fifty matches: 0.6 yuan per hundred boxes; 4) Each box containing more than fifty but no more than seventy-five matches: 0.9 yuan per hundred boxes. For each additional twenty-five matches or part thereof per box: 0.3 yuan per hundred boxes. (E) Edible Oils and Fats 1) Peanut oil, also known as groundnut oil: 0.04 yuan per pound. British goods are 0.02 yuan; 2) Canned butter: 0.17 yuan per pound. British goods are only 0.12 yuan; 3) Chilled beef: 0.2 yuan per pound. British goods are only 0.15 yuan; 4) Margarine: 0.1 yuan per pound. British goods are only 0.05 yuan; 5) Lard: 0.04 yuan per pound; 6) Indian cheese, vegetable oil, and other edible oils (excluding coconut oil): 0.1 yuan per pound. (F) Red clay ash: 12 yuan per ton. British goods are only 6 yuan; (G) Objects made of red clay ash (excluding floor tiles and roof tiles): 2 yuan per ton; (H) Bricks and Tiles 1) Roof tiles: 12 yuan per ton; 2) Floor tiles: 12 yuan per ton. British goods are 10 yuan; (I) Cosmetics and Perfumes: 50 percent of the price. British goods are 25 percent; (J) Woven fabrics and clothing 1) Whether or not made into objects, all cotton, linen, jute, silk, rayon, felt, wool, and other fabrics (excluding thread and burlap bags): 20 percent of the price. British goods are only 10 percent; 2) Clothing: 20 percent of the price. British goods are only 10 percent; 3) Rubber shoes or canvas shoes with rubber soles: 0.5 yuan per pair. British goods are only 0.1 yuan. (Note: This is the newly revised tax rate) 4) Rubber shoe soles: 0.25 yuan per pair. British goods are only 0.05 yuan; (K) Objects made of leather and imitation leather (excluding luxury items): 10 percent of the price; (L) Peanuts, also known as groundnuts: 0.02 yuan per pound. British goods are only 0.01 yuan; (M) Fruits, jams, vegetables, fish, meat, and soups packaged in iron cans, glass jars, or clay bottles: 20 percent of the price. British goods are only 5 percent; (N) Manufactured copperware, both raw and processed: 15 percent of the price. British goods are only 5 percent; (O) Raw and processed leather: 15 percent of the price. British goods are only 5 percent; (P) Fish maw and shark fin: 15 percent of the price. British goods are only 5 percent; (Q) Umbrellas and lampshades with covers made of silk, rayon, or cotton cloth: 10 percent of the price. British goods are only 5 yuan.

After being detected by the authorities, an arrest warrant was issued. Cai, realizing the failure, fled to Hong Kong for refuge. He was arrested, interrogated, and imprisoned for one year by the Hong Kong government. Upon completing his sentence, he was expelled from the concession. The Guangdong Provincial Public Security Bureau discovered the arrest warrant and dispatched Chen Xingfan to track Cai Jun, who boarded the Empress of Asia on the 6th of this month, and came to Shanghai. Prior to this, the bureau telegraphed the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau to request assistance with the arrest. After reading the telegram, Director Wen ordered Inspector Cai and officers from the Water Patrol to rush to the ship at Wusongkou. Upon entering port, the ship was inspected, and Cai Jun was immediately arrested and taken to the bureau. After an interrogation by the Third Section, the Guangdong Public Security Bureau was notified of the arrest. Yesterday (the 11th) around 10 AM, Director Wen approved the handover of Cai to officers from the Guangdong bureau, who escorted him to the Qingyuan Steamer of the Dong Tai Koo Company at Xin Kaihe and returned him for trial. It is reported that Director Wen ordered the Criminal Investigation Team to send squad leader Hu Kuisheng and Detective Rong Bingchen, along with three others, to escort him on board to prevent any unforeseen circumstances.

Recent News on the Chen Duxiu Case 189

After Chen Duxiu was arrested, he was handed over to the Nanjing District Court for detention. Following the precedent of the Noulens case, the High Court has jurisdiction over the first instance. Chief Judge Wang of the High Court appointed Prosecutor Li to handle the case. The court has already held two hearings. Chen Duxiu specially selected Zhang Shizhao and Guo Weiran as his lawyers. On the 7th, he sent a letter urging Lawyer Guo to come to Beijing for a meeting. Lawyer Guo took the express train to Beijing on the night of the 8th. At 11 AM on the morning of the 9th, Chen signed a contract entrusting Lawyer Guo with his defense. Fearing that he would be lonely in detention, Lawyer Guo presented him with four copies of Guo Wei's "General Principles of Criminal Law" and ten yuan in cash for his use. Lawyer Guo returned to Shanghai on the morning of the 10th. It is reported that the two lawyers discussed the defense strategy the previous night.

More Japanese Naval Troops Arrive 190

More officers and soldiers continue to arrive. The Japanese Navy Ministry had previously sent 625 marines and incorporated them into Shanghai. A telegram was received stating that an additional 250 naval soldiers will be sent to Shanghai to augment various ships of the First Foreign Expeditionary Fleet of the Yangtze River. They are expected to arrive in Shanghai on the Qingdao warship on the 22nd. These soldiers will then be assigned to various Japanese warships on the Yangtze River. Yesterday afternoon, the Navy Ministry also sent a large group of mid-level Japanese naval officers, including Hirata Kiichi, Uemura Yoshitaro, Kobata Morizo, Urata, Itaguchi, Kawamoto Hiroshi, Kamo Yao, Sugata, Endo Tsune, Tabata Suke, Tsurutori, Kawada, Sekihei, Mine Ken, Sakamoto, Kato, and more than thirty others, who have been assigned to the Shanghai Marine Corps and have already arrived in Shanghai.

▲ Saito Goes to Dalian. Lieutenant General Saito of the Japanese Navy Veterans Association, who came from Shanghai to inspect various ports along the Yangtze River and Nanjing, has completed his tasks and returned to Shanghai. Yesterday, he purchased a ticket on the Fengtian Maru and left Shanghai at 9 AM to travel to Dalian and then to various parts of the Northeast.

▲Enlisted Men Return Home. Warrant officers within the Japanese Naval Landing Forces who participated in the fighting in Shanghai have now received orders from the Navy Ministry to be promoted and transferred back to Japan. With the exception of Commander Sakoiji and the new commander of the Third Fleet, Yonai, who must come to Shanghai before they can return home, First Lieutenant Imada Sho, and Ensigns Suenaga, Takao, Oonaka, Nakamura, Fujimoto, Kobayashi, Shigemura, Tanabe, Takatsuka, Tomoda, Asanaga, etc., have been promoted to lieutenant and will return home on the Shanghai Maru tomorrow. It is also reported that Mayor Wu of our country will host a farewell banquet for Sakoiji on Monday, with the presidents of various Japanese companies in Shanghai, such as Mitsubishi, Mitsui, Nippon Yusen Kaisha, Nissin, and Osaka, invited as guests.

The Hubei Public Association 191

Opposes Liu Zhennian's Troops Being Transferred to Hubei

The Shanghai Hubei Public Association telegraphed the Central Government to oppose the transfer of Liu Zhennian's troops to central Hubei: "Your Excellency (a respectful form of address), Hubei has suffered from natural disasters and man-made calamities for a long time. Famine has struck repeatedly, bandits and communists are rampant, and displacement and chaos prevail, leaving most homes empty. Fortunately, Chairman Chiang, mindful of the suffering of the disaster victims, is determined to suppress the communists. The fighting has brought peace and stability. From the five illustrations in the 'Pictorial Record of Communist Suppression' published in the Hankou Zhen Dan Bao, it is clear that the Xu, He, and Kong factions have been wiped out. Only small, scattered remnants remain, occupying less than one county and possessing fewer than one thousand guns. This proves that the efforts to suppress the communists in Hubei have been successful. The military phase has passed, and what is needed now is political relief for the displaced and stability for the people. Since the suppression of the communists began, large armies have gathered, and the main force of the communists has been crushed without any remnants. Using them to search for the remaining bandits would be more than sufficient. There is no need to transfer troops from other provinces to Hubei to assist in the suppression. Liu Zhennian's troops are stationed in Jiaodong, where they levy taxes indiscriminately, oppress the people to the bone, and have no military discipline. Chairman Han punished them first, and then the people of Jiaodong enumerated their crimes. Their oppressive policies and domineering actions are well-known to the people of the country. Recently, news reports stated that the Central Government mediated the Shandong affair and decided to transfer Liu Zhennian's troops to central Hubei to suppress the communists, which is alarming. Hubei has recovered its lost territory, the displaced have returned, and the priority is political stability. To place troops who are accustomed to cruelty and oppression over people who have just recovered from pain is tantamount to poisoning a sick person, depriving the people of Hubei of any hope of recovery. This association, concerned about its homeland, cannot stand by and watch. With a heart of saving our hometown, we make an earnest appeal to ensure that Liu Zhennian's troops are transferred to areas where the work of suppressing the communists is intense, so that they can redeem themselves through meritorious service, which would benefit the country and the people, not only directly benefiting Hubei but also indirectly benefiting the country. Respectfully submitted by the Shanghai Hubei Public Association."

Japanese Trade Statistics with Foreign Countries and China 192

Total Exports in October

The office of the Japanese Commercial Counselor in Shanghai received a telegram from Japan yesterday stating that Japan's total exports in October were worth 147,000,000 Japanese yen. Exports such as raw silk, cotton cloth, and miscellaneous goods increased, resulting in a trade surplus of 49,000,000 Japanese yen. However, the total foreign trade for the ten months since January is still a trade deficit of 66,000,000 Japanese yen, an increase of 11,000,000 Japanese yen compared to the same period last year. The current export trade situation is quite good and is expected to improve the balance. Exports to China in September were worth 13,000,000 Japanese yen, resulting in a trade surplus of 6,000,000 Japanese yen (which, in our country's terms, is a trade deficit). Compared to the export value of the same period last year, exports to North China increased by 58 percent, while exports to Central China decreased by 37 percent, and exports to South China decreased by 63 percent. As for Chinese goods imported into Japan, imports from North China increased by 5.7 percent, imports from Central China increased by 1.7 percent, and imports from South China decreased by 12.8 percent. Exports from Japan to the three northeastern provinces in September were worth 14,000,000 Japanese yen, resulting in a trade surplus of 9,500,000 Japanese yen. Compared to the same period last year, exports increased by 100 percent and imports decreased by 37 percent.

Shanghai Storytelling Competition 193

Starts Today

Preparations for the first Shanghai Bureau of Education-sponsored Storytelling Competition have been completed. A total of 51 storytellers from Guangyu Society, Runyu Society, the Yangzhou Group, and others have registered to participate, with 39 different programs. Kidnappers Commit Murder in Yuyao 194

Return to Shanghai for Extortion

Former Tahe Comprador Shen Chengfu is Extorted

The Bandits Agreed to Use Cigarette Tins as Signals

The Police Sent Detectives to Lie in Wait and Arrested Six People

They Were Interrogated Yesterday and Sent to Yuyao for Trial

Shen Chengfu, a Yuyao native who formerly served as the comprador of the British Tahe Foreign Firm, lost his comprador position last year after losing a large sum of money in speculative business ventures. The Zhihe Qianzhuang managed by his father, Shen Yingxiang, was also dragged down by the issuance of bad checks and went bankrupt. A few months ago, while Shen Yingxiang, who was also unemployed, had returned to his ancestral home in Wucheyan, Yuyao, he and his family were attentively watching a theatrical performance held to honor the gods. Suddenly, several thugs silently approached and opened fire on him with pistols. Shen Yingxiang's second son, Shanfu, rushed forward upon hearing the alarm, protecting his father with his sister, but was fatally shot on the spot. Yingxiang and his daughter were both wounded by gunfire, and the assailants escaped. It was later learned that the thugs were notorious kidnappers who believed Yingxiang had made a fortune in Shanghai and returned home with a large sum of money, so they attempted to kidnap him for ransom. However, the local authorities were conducting a strict manhunt, so the bandits fled to Shanghai, still obsessed with the Shen family. Recently, they learned of Shen Chengfu's address and sent him a threatening letter demanding 50,000 yuan. They initially arranged to negotiate at a hotel on Avenue Edward VII, but later changed the meeting place to in front of the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association on Tibet Road at 1:30 PM on November 3. Those attending would carry three cigarette tins as a signal. Shen immediately reported this information to the Old Gate Police Station. Detectives Zhou Guisen and Zhang Yi were dispatched to the meeting place to observe the situation. Soon after, Xing Weicheng from Shaoxing arrived and was arrested. Under interrogation, they proceeded to house number 357 on Rue Tenant de la Tour in the French Concession, where they arrested five other people: Wang Jianfa, Sun Yiqian, Song Yixin, Wang Jixiang, and a woman named Wang Qiu. They were handed over to the First Special District Court. They confessed that there were other accomplices at large, and they were ordered to be detained pending the arrest of the remaining bandits. A week has passed, and no other fugitives have been apprehended. The Yuyao County Government, after investigation, discovered that the Xing group were the wanted criminals who had shot and killed Shen Shanfu and his father. They prepared an official letter and sent police to Shanghai to request their extradition. This morning, they petitioned the court to transfer the suspects. Judge Qian ordered the suspects to be brought before the court for interrogation. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that the police investigation revealed that the arrested suspects had only committed extortion against Shen Chengfu and had not committed any other crimes. Therefore, the police had no objection to the Yuyao authorities' request for extradition. Judge Qian then ordered that the six men and women, including Xing Weicheng, be handed over to the police from the Yuyao County Government for return and trial.

Two Kidnappers Executed by Firing Squad 195

Xia Adi Said Goodbye to His Family

Tears Flowed, a Sad Sight

Dong Shuying was kidnapped by bandits on Avenue Joffre on May 27 of this year. The General Investigation Section of the General Police Department arrested several kidnappers, including Shanghai native Xia Adi (29 years old) and Zheng Gengsheng (24 years old), and handed them over to the First Special District Court. After clear confession and judgement, the two criminals Xia and Zheng were sentenced to death and reported to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval and execution. Yesterday afternoon, the time for execution arrived. The police escorted the two criminals to the case hearing. The execution magistrate Shen Shanzeng, presided over the Third Criminal Court. He explained to the two criminals that they had been ordered to be executed by firing squad today and asked if they had any last words. Xia Adi stated that his parents and wife were in court today and requested permission to have a final conversation to express his farewell. The court granted permission. Xia then said to his wife and parents, "I will be executed today. You must go to the execution ground to collect my body. I was foolishly deceived by others in this matter, and I regret it, but it is too late. Please, parents, take care of my wife and handle all unfinished matters." As he spoke, tears flowed down his face, and the scene was very sad. Zheng Gengsheng then stated that he had a suit of Western clothing and eighteen pawn tickets at the police station, and he requested that a letter be sent to his wife, Zheng Hemei, at number 1412 next to the Dahua Hotel on Avenue Edward VII, asking her to come and collect them. He had nothing else to say. After reviewing the confession, Magistrate Shen ordered them to be sent to the Prosecutor's Office of the District Court for execution. Chinese and Western police officers escorted the two criminals down, together with the photo file, and loaded them into a car that drove directly to the Pujiangjing execution ground. At the same time, the District Court was notified to send a prosecutor to supervise the execution along with the bailiff. After questioning the two criminals one last time, they were ordered to be executed by firing squad.

Anhui Public Associations Oppose the Rice Surtax 196

Representatives Depart for Beiping and Tianjin

It was heard yesterday that the Anhui Fellow Villagers and Anhui Academic Association in Shanghai are opposing the rice surtax. Although the National Government has expressed its intention to abolish it, Wu Zhongxin, Ye Yuanlong, and Jiang Wei have not immediately canceled it. Yesterday, they sent representatives Xia Junhuan to depart for Beiping, Tianjin, and other places to appeal to and connect with fellow villagers, jointly opposing the tax until the goal of abolishing it is achieved. The representatives were heard to have boarded a train north from the station at 7:00 AM yesterday.

Northeast Refugee Association to Ship Cotton Clothes 197

The Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Relief Association for Northeast Refugees yesterday received a telegram from its representatives in Beiping, Qu Yingguang and Feng Xuefen, which stated, "The relief funds received include 50,000 yuan, which were first transferred to the Bank of China, Changchun branch. Only 6,000 pieces of cotton clothing have been transported to Beiping. Are these suits or just upper garments? This amount is very disappointing. There are many disaster victims from the Northeast arriving in Beiping. It would be best to find ways to increase aid. Feng is expected to leave the customs on the (14th). Changchun has approved an additional 30,000 sets of clothing, which requires an additional 50,000 yuan. Please also remit the Harbin relief funds successively, as postal correspondence is slow and delayed, and we are deeply concerned about delays. The Beiping porridge kitchens are scheduled to open simultaneously on the (16th). We will wait for proper arrangements here, then return to Shanghai via Qingdao." After receiving the telegram, the association plans to pack and ship the more than 7,000 pieces of cotton clothing currently in stock, of which half are cotton pants and 10% are children's clothes, dividing and sending 50% to each of Changchun and Harbin.

Since its establishment, the Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Relief Association for Northeast Refugees has actively solicited donations for relief efforts. The amount of relief funds remitted daily is considerable. Yesterday, the association received an advance of 3,000 yuan from Jisheng Hospital and 2,400 yuan from Lianyi Shanhui, which were remitted to Beiping yesterday morning to provide relief.

The Shanghai Flour Exchange yesterday sent a letter to Renji Tang on Six Malu, the Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Relief Association for Northeast Refugees, and the Provisional Relief Association for Disaster Areas in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, stating that the Shanghai Flour Exchange will donate 1.5% of its business revenue to disaster relief, for a period of six months. Approximately 1,000 taels of silver will be donated each month. 1,000 silver dollars will be sent this month for the relief of Northeast refugees, but the assistance will be divided such that four months will be spent on relieving the Northeast, and two months on helping the disaster areas of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces. It is reported that the association has already received the 1,000 taels for Northeast relief in advance.

Establishment of the Shanghai Russian Emigrant Association 200

Kotenev is Appointed Chairman

Although There is No Extraterritoriality, Foreigners Also Receive Equal Treatment

Last Sunday (i.e., the 6th of this month), the Shanghai Russian Emigrant Public United Association was formally established at its headquarters at No. 39 Avenue Edward VII, Shanghai. The establishment of the association was submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters for registration, and the Municipal Party Headquarters approved its establishment in its approvals of August 4 and October 8 of this year. On the day of the association's inaugural meeting, 39 representatives from 33 Russian emigrant associations, plus one representative from the "Shanghai General Russian Association," attended. The members of the aforementioned Russian emigrant associations total 3,000, and averaging three relatives per Russian emigrant, the total number of people should be 9,000. From this, it can be seen that the newly established Shanghai Russian Emigrant Public United Association is an organization that represents the majority of Russian emigrants, as the household survey statistics show that there are a total of 15,000 Russian emigrants in Shanghai. The leader of the United Association is A.M. Kotenev, a famous jurist who has served in the Secretariat of the Shanghai Municipal Council for many years and has considerable affection for our country. Therefore, his leadership of the United Association will be based on compliance with our country's laws as a prerequisite. The efforts of Mr. Guo have contributed to the ability of Shanghai's Russian emigrants to abide by our laws and recognize our country's authority in public life. However, recently, a small group of Russian emigrant organizations, led by CH. Metzler (Mr. Metzler was the secretary of the former Russian Imperial Consulate in Shanghai), under the name "Shanghai Russian Emigrant Relief Society," located at No. 6 Hong Kong Road, is still attacking and calling the United Association pro-foreign and treasonous. On the day of the United Association's official inaugural meeting, the Relief Society's Russian-language newspaper Slovo published a vitriolic editorial attacking Mr. Guo as a communist and warning Russian emigrants not to join the United Association, implying that the association was under the control of the Kuomintang, and that the most likely outcome was that all Russian emigrants in the association would become communists. Various unsightly slogans and cartoons were published in the newspaper, representing the Kuomintang as Mongolian barbarians, and Mr. Guo as unable to supply plans. Before and on the day of the association's official establishment, it was subjected to various abuses, and even anonymous letters were sent to the leaders of other foreign organizations in an attempt to destroy it. However, the United Association's official inaugural meeting was successfully held. The following are the elected executive committee members of the United Association: Chairman Kotenev, Vice Chairman Sentelikov, Doctor Fumin, Secretary He Leci, and Doctor Accountant Bokemian. All of these individuals are foreigners who are friendly to our country and abide by the law. The preferential treatment given to Shanghai's Russian emigrants by the Chinese Kuomintang proves that foreigners, although without extraterritorial rights, also receive equal treatment under the law. This further refutes the fallacy in the Lytton Report that White Russian emigrants in the three northeastern provinces receive poor treatment from China.

The Shanghai Municipal Council Will Print a New Shanghai Map 201

Permission Granted for J.D. Fage Bookstore to Print

The Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council has recently completed the revision of the map of Shanghai and its surrounding areas. Compared to the old map, the scope of the northern district has been greatly expanded, and the eastern boundary has also been slightly lengthened. The Director of the Public Works Department believes that it would be very expensive to print the map abroad. If J.D. Fage Bookstore in Shanghai were to undertake the printing, the printing costs could be saved, and the work would be satisfactory. This matter has been approved by the Public Works Committee and the Board of Directors. The printing cost is estimated at 4,050 yuan. After publication, a certain amount of revenue can be obtained from sales to offset the costs.

Difficult to Expand the Pond in Hongkew Park for the Time Being 202

Recently, several people have written letters to the Western newspapers, advocating for the construction of a pond in Hongkew Park for model boats to sail in. According to the Public Works Committee's consideration, it is not appropriate to convert the existing pond for this purpose. The Acting Director of the Public Works Department reported that the depth of the existing pond is not suitable, and the small bushes along the pond are needed for wind protection and are important for the scenery of the entire park, so they cannot be removed. The pond should not be remodeled according to the wishes of a few people. After deliberation, the committee recommended that the pond remain as it is, but an item can be included in next year's budget to prepare for the construction of a model boat pond. However, it is questionable whether there will be sufficient financial resources next year. This suggestion has been adopted by the Board of Directors.

Funeral of the President of the Dongjiadu Fire Department 203

Shen Guoliang's Funeral Tomorrow

Shen Guopu, President of the Dongjiadu Fire Department, has always been enthusiastic about serving the community. He has been running around raising funds for fire prevention for 20 years. He is respected by the local people. This autumn, while inspecting fire departments in the north, his car passed through Shandong. He took the opportunity to visit Mount Tai and fell into the Black Dragon Pool, losing his life. Fortunately, Feng Yuxiang helped to retrieve his body, which was simply coffined and transported south, and temporarily placed in the Fire Department. The funeral will be held tomorrow morning, first at the Fire Department for a memorial service, and then at 2:00 PM, the funeral procession will depart and be buried at the Zobeigen Road Bubbling Well Cemetery. The memorial groups include the South Shanghai District Defense Corps, the Fire Brigade Joint Association, the Qiuxin Factory, the Xuhui Public School Alumni Association, the Catholic Action Society, the Music Association, etc. In addition to relatives and friends, those assisting the coffin include Shanghai Middle School Boy Scouts, members of the South Shanghai District Defense Corps, and members of the Zhabei and South Shanghai District Fire Brigades.

Chen Jieqing Enshrined in the Haichang Guildhall 204

Chen Jieqing, a prominent member of the Haiyan family, passed away suddenly this spring after suffering a minor illness. Chen served as an official in Shanghai for 40 years, with his achievements well-known. After retiring, he lived in seclusion in Shanghai and was elected as a director of the China Law Society Suzhou Orphans' Home and chairman of the Haiyan Fellow-Villagers Association. He was particularly enthusiastic about local public welfare and charitable undertakings. It is reported that his fellow villagers from Haiyan residing in Shanghai, in remembrance of his achievements, have decided to hold a public ceremony at noon on the 13th of this month to enshrine Chen's spirit tablet in the Sage Shrine of the Haichang Guildhall, in order to commend him.

Yesterday, Mr. Sun Zhesheng, accompanied by Zhang Huichang, Chen Ce, Ma Chaojun, Jian Youwen, Wang Zhiyuan, and others, visited the factory. They all greatly praised the factory's methods and products, and personally inscribed words such as "Industrially Saving the Country." Reply from the Taxpayers' Association to the Western Clothing Industry 208

Regarding the Opposition to Telephone Rate Increases

The increase in telephone rates in the concession has sparked public outcry. Disputes have continued to this day, with no concrete solution. The Western Clothing Industry Association recently sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, urging them to persevere to the end. The Taxpayers' Association yesterday sent a letter in reply, detailing the progress of negotiations. The full text of the correspondence is as follows: (1) Esteemed Sirs, the matter of the Shanghai telephone rate increase has been widely publicized since July of this year, causing a great uproar. A small number of subscribers have carelessly resigned themselves to it without considering the consequences, and have been unknowingly pressured into compliance. Subsequently, public organizations such as the First District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' Association and the Nanjing Road Business Association have repeatedly argued against the rate increase, citing reasons and issuing public statements of protest, which we believe your association has already noted. In view of the economic conditions of this city, our association finds it difficult to bear such a burden. We have long admired your association's upholding of justice. We have read with respect your association's letter to the Public Works Department, which was stern, righteous, and hit the mark, deeply resonating with the public sentiment. We sincerely hope that your association will persevere to the end, show sympathy and support, and vow to achieve the termination of the original telephone rate increase proposal. This would be a great boon to merchants and residents alike. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association. (2) Esteemed Sirs, we acknowledge receipt of your letter of November 5 regarding the telephone rate increase, which is incompatible with the social economy, and your request that we persevere in opposing it to the end. Upon receiving news of the telephone rate increase, our association immediately wrote to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, explaining that under the circumstances of the social economy, the rate increase was unacceptable, and requesting that it be temporarily postponed. Unexpectedly, not only was this not approved, but the Public Works Department even went so far as to violate the universally recognized legal principle against retroactive application, adding charges retroactively from March 27 onwards. This led to widespread opposition. In accordance with public opinion, our association actively explained to the Public Works Department the reasons for opposing the rate increase and demanding its immediate cancellation. When the First District Branch of the Citizens' Association and the Nanjing Road Business Association issued a declaration, we immediately forwarded it to the Public Works Department, urging them to submit it to the Board of Directors for reconsideration along with our case. In response to the above, we respectfully reply to your association, hoping you will take note and offer your valuable guidance to correct any shortcomings. This is our sincere prayer. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Western Clothing Industry Association.

One Person Kidnapped on the Dongsheng Steamer Ransomed 210

The Dongsheng, a North China-bound steamer of Jardine Matheson, was traveling to Tanggu last month when its compradore, Li Shanting, was kidnapped by bandits on board. Wharf manager Huang Wenqi and a Mr. Zhang who stepped forward to stop them were also abducted. After this incident occurred, the British Consul in Tianjin negotiated with the Tianjin authorities for their rescue. At the same time, the families of the hostages also sought rescue through various channels. Later, it was discovered that the hostages were being held in Xinzhuang, near Tianjin. The family of Huang Wenqi negotiated with the bandits repeatedly and eventually ransomed Huang Wenqi for 20,000 yuan. Subsequently, the military learned of this and dispatched troops to suppress the bandits, but the bandits had already moved the hostages, including Li Shanting, to another location. According to Huang Wenqi, Li Shanting had become deranged due to severe stress and his whereabouts are currently unknown. His family is extremely anxious.

Late-Blooming Chrysanthemums at the Garden Farm Distributed by Lottery 211

After the closing of the chrysanthemum exhibition at the Jinggou Municipal Garden Farm on the 7th, there were still many beautiful potted and upright chrysanthemums, in addition to those that were donated or distributed. There are also late-blooming prized varieties that are still opening. A new area has now been opened to display them in categories, so that citizens can visit and admire them. If there are any items you like, you can still purchase them at a low price. There is also a lottery distribution method, with each ticket costing one yuan, guaranteeing at least four pots and up to twenty pots, or two large upright chrysanthemums, which is very cheap. Those with a penchant for Yuanming's chrysanthemum can visit the farm freely this Sunday (November 13) before 1:00 PM.

Yang Xixian Purchases Cotton with Bad Checks 212

Court Orders Arrest; Yang Surrenders

Yesterday's Trial Orders Release on 10,000 Yuan Bail

Yang Xixian, a local resident who lives at No. 42 Xin Chongqing Road, holds the position of manager at Longmao Textile Co., Ltd. Recently, the company suddenly went bankrupt due to financial difficulties. It then hired lawyer Li Zuyu and accountant Xu Yongzu to publish a notice to settle accounts. However, on September 28 of this year, Yang, in the name of the company, ordered 100 bales of cotton from the Mei'an Foreign Firm at No. 4 Edward Road, valued at 14,316 taels and 7 cents. Two checks were issued to the Zhongnan Bank for payment on a future date. When the foreign firm went to Zhongnan Bank to collect the money on the due date, it was discovered that Longmao Company had no funds, and the checks were returned. Subsequently, the Mei'an Foreign Firm negotiated with Longmao, but Yang avoided meeting them. After a thorough investigation, it was discovered that the cotton had been mortgaged by Yang to Zhongnan Bank to obtain funds for his escape, which constituted intentional fraud. The foreign firm then reported the matter to the General Police Station, which forwarded it to the First Special District Court, which issued an arrest warrant. Until the day before yesterday, Yang realized that he could not escape the law and surrendered to the police. He was detained by the police chief and sent to the Summary Court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. In addition to sending Deputy Manager Zhang Qiankui to court to respond to the lawsuit, the victim, Mei'an Foreign Firm, also hired lawyer Zhu Xiyun to appear in court to file a civil suit, requesting that the court order compensation for the losses. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated that the police were prosecuting the defendant under Article 363 of the Criminal Law for fraud and breach of trust, and described how Yang Xixian defrauded Mei'an Foreign Firm of goods by fraudulent means, alleging that the defendant specialized in purchasing goods from various foreign firms and businesses with bad checks and then mortgaging the goods to banks to obtain funds for hiding. He added that there were likely many such cases of fraud, and the police were currently investigating. It was also discovered that Longmao Company had mortgaged 250,000 taels to Zhongnan Bank. Therefore, he requested that the case be adjourned for a special hearing. The defendant, who had hired lawyer Zhang Zhengju to appear in court, agreed to the adjournment but requested that the arrest warrant be revoked and that the defendant be allowed to be released on bail. After consulting with Judge Liu Yugui, it was ruled that the case would be rescheduled for a further hearing next Friday afternoon, and Yang Xixian was allowed to be released on 10,000 taels bail, with the defense lawyer responsible for ensuring his attendance when summoned.

Case of Jiao Daosong and Wang Aoxi 213

Jiao Daosong Transferred to Public Security Bureau First

The case of Jiao Daosong, advisor to the Military Affairs Committee, and Wang Aoxi, former chief writer for the New World News, who were arrested at the China Hotel by personnel from the Municipal Public Security Bureau in conjunction with the Lao Zha Police for suspected reactionary activities and detained for interrogation by the Second Branch of the High Court, has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the Second Branch of the High Court, with Judge Yu presiding, continued the trial in a collegial panel. The Municipal Public Security Bureau specially dispatched legal counsel Zhan Jifeng to court to request the transfer of Jiao Daosong. Subsequently, police lawyer Li Zhishan stated that during the extension period, the police had seized a number of documents at No. 7 Gongping Road, all of which were related to Wang Aoxi. These documents were still under investigation, so he requested another extension for review. Lawyer Zhan stated that the Public Security Bureau's request for an extension regarding Wang Aoxi could be agreed to, but since there were no new facts discovered regarding Jiao Daosong, he should be allowed to be transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation first, so as not to delay the process. After consultation with assessors Zhao and Lu, Judge Yu deemed this to be reasonable and immediately ruled that Jiao Daosong should be transferred to the Public Security Bureau for investigation, while Wang Aoxi would be returned to custody, and the trial would be continued on the morning of the 21st of this month.

Robbery on Xin Dagu Road Yesterday Morning 214

Yesterday (November 11th) at around 8:00 AM, two thugs suddenly broke into the home of a certain family at No. 55 Yongqingfang, Xin Dagu Road in the Public Concession. They were aggressive and intimidating, and after some threats, they robbed the family of clothing and cash totaling over 300 yuan, and also took two pistols that the victim possessed. The victim reported the incident to the Xin Zha Police Station, who ordered officers to conduct a thorough investigation.

Jiading Police Officers Tian Yu Sentenced 215

Tian Zhihe, director of the Jiading County Public Security Bureau branch, and Yu Taiji, captain of the General Bureau's Detective Team, were found guilty of conspiring to defraud villagers of 500 yuan for personal use. These acts implicated Police Chief Zhu Shouzhi, and were therefore transferred by the county government to the Jiangsu High Court for a ruling, which designated the Shanghai District Court to manage the first instance. After the prosecutor concluded the investigation, Zhu Shouzhi was dismissed without prosecution, while Tian Zhihe and Yu Taiji were prosecuted for accepting bribes. After repeated questioning by the criminal court, Tian Zhihe and Yu Taiji were each sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 500 yuan. In addition, 150 yuan of the embezzled money should be recovered from Tian Zhihe and 350 yuan from Yu Taiji, and confiscated for public use.

Central Bank Inspection Report 216

142nd Report

The 142nd inspection report on the Central Bank's issuance reserves states: "In accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the Bank's issuance of convertible banknotes. On November 10, 1932, Wang Yihou conducted the 142nd inspection at the Bank's Issuance Bureau. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) Total value of convertible banknotes issued: 31,878,171 silver dollars, including 28,481,820 silver dollar notes and 3,396,351 subsidiary currency dollars. Total reserve funds for convertible banknotes: 31,878,171 silver dollars, including 26,149,171 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve consists of 23,137,236.16 yuan stored in the Bank's Issuance Vault, 1,790,950 yuan stored in branches in various ports, and 1,220,984.84 yuan deposited with other banks. The security reserve is equivalent to 5,729,000 silver dollars. (B) Total value of customs gold convertible banknotes issued: 425,000 yuan. Total reserve funds for customs gold convertible banknotes: 425,000 yuan. This reserve consists of 170,000 US dollars deposited with local banks. At the fixed price of 40 to 1 customs gold, this equals 425,000 yuan. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the security reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the security reserve is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. November 10, 1932, Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank."

Jiangwan Hospital Plans to Continue Operations 223

Jiangwan Epidemic Hospital has been operating for nearly ten years. Last year, a local gentleman, Zhu Jiansheng, donated more than three mu of land to build a new building, which gradually stabilized the foundation. Unexpectedly, the January 28th Incident occurred, and the entire building was destroyed. With the enthusiastic donations of philanthropists Zhu Ziyun, Cai Xiangsun, Zhang Xinliang, Wang Hanli, Quan Yuanren, and others, as well as the Xu Bingji Construction Factory and the hospital's board of directors, a new building was rebuilt. The hospital mainly treats epidemic diseases during the summer and autumn, and during normal times, it is converted into an obstetrics department and also handles common diseases. However, the hospital is a charity that provides free treatment to the poor, and its finances are quite tight. Last night, a dinner was held at the Sichuan Road YMCA to entertain philanthropists, including Zhu Ziyun, Cai Xiangsun, and the heads of various departments of the hospital, Dr. Wang Enguang. Mr. Wang Hanli, the hospital's representative, hosted the event. During the dinner, Mr. Wang described the hospital's current situation and future plans. He stated that if the hospital could not continue to operate, the poor and sick would suffer greatly, and he hoped that all philanthropists would provide substantial assistance so that the hospital could continue to operate without interruption.

In addition to the existing preparations by Zhang Wuyuan and others, Luo Jue, a former business leader, has also been hired to actively prepare and strive for perfection. As for the opening date, due to the upcoming winter vacation and the limited amount of teaching time, it will be changed to open in the spring of next year.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast for 4:30 PM yesterday stated: "The weather in Shandong and the Yellow Sea is clear and cold, with strong northwesterly winds. The weather along the coast here and south of Ma'an Island is cold and cloudy, with gusts or strong northerly to northeasterly winds. The Yangtze River basin is clear, with northwesterly winds. The weather in southern Taiwan is extremely bad due to a hurricane, the center of which, at around 6:00 AM this morning, had moved to within 60 miles of the intersection of 16 degrees north latitude and 123 degrees east longitude, with extremely strong winds, moving northwestward. Also, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 63.7 degrees and the lowest was 58.1 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 61.2 degrees and the lowest was 56.3 degrees."

Letter to the Editor 227

Esteemed Sirs, in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on November 10th, there was a news item titled "Huishan Police Station Seizes Large Number of Kidnappers," which included a criminal named "Zhou Yuanlong from Qingjiang." This coincidentally matches my hometown and name. I live in Yangshupu and have been teaching for many years. I am sincerely concerned that inaccurate rumors will spread and damage my reputation. I am writing this letter to clarify the matter and request that you publish this letter in the "Letters to the Editor" column. Thank you. Respectfully, Zhou Yuanlong, 492 Huasheng Road, Yangshupu, November 11th.

Special Delivery

Judge Fessenden's Research on the Shanghai International Settlement 228

Report Volume IV (20)

12. The aforementioned regulations regarding pensions apparently conform to the statutory permanent service. If employees can maintain proper conduct, they can retain their positions, except in the event of certain types of incidents, until they have served for twenty years and reached the age of fifty. Furthermore, if such an incident occurs, they also have the right to claim compensation. However, in reality, the employees of the Public Works Department do not enjoy such legal rights. According to the three-year contract system, the Public Works Department can refuse to renew the contract of any employee at any time, regardless of how close they are to being eligible for a pension, and regardless of any hardship they may experience as a result of losing the opportunity to receive a pension. The employee has no legal basis to file a complaint. The situation is the same under the newly established contract format, because even if an employee is only slightly more than six months away from becoming eligible for a pension, the Public Works Department can still terminate the contract at any time with six months' notice. Employees who lose their opportunity to receive a pension due to such notice, and not due to their own fault, have no legal basis to file a complaint.

13. In fact, it has been the policy of the Public Works Department to treat its employees fairly. The department has never used its legal powers in an unreasonable manner to deprive its employees of their pensions when they are close to being eligible for them. However, given the conditions attached to Clause 24 of the already cited Land Regulations, it seems that when establishing the current pension system, the Public Works Department should have taken the natural step of enacting a provision that allows foreign employees to continue in their positions after a probationary period until they reach the age at which they can receive a pension. However, if it is necessary to dismiss an employee before they reach the age at which they can receive a pension for the sake of departmental affairs, the department retains the right to dismiss them. If the dismissal is not due to the employee's incompetence or poor performance, then compensation can be given according to reasonable standards, or including a portion of the pension calculated proportionally to the years of service.

14. Currently, a peculiar situation arises because the legal rights actually possessed by the Public Works Department's employees are inconsistent with the so-called moral or reasonable demands that have been customarily recognized by the Public Works Department. If the department does not recognize these demands, it is inconsistent with the entire principle of adopting a pension system.

D. The Need for Security of Tenure

15. In the previous chapter of this report (Note 5), it was solemnly stated that one of the main elements for the Public Works Department to establish an honest and effective administration is to provide its employees with generous remuneration and security of tenure.

16. Regarding this, security of tenure is extremely important. Although many employees have served in the Public Works Department for a long time and have therefore received pensions, a system that is originally intended to establish permanent service but does not provide any guarantee of permanence to the relevant employees, and that allows questions regarding security of tenure and pension rights to be handled entirely at the discretion of the authorities without being based on accepted and approved conditions, cannot be considered satisfactory.

17. Although the issue of security of tenure arises primarily from the current status of foreign employees, since only foreign employees are covered by the current pension system, it may soon be deemed appropriate to make necessary modifications to the measures established for the benefit of foreign employees and extend them to senior Chinese staff, as the Public Works Department is increasingly adopting a policy of increasing the number of senior Chinese staff.

18. In this way, the scope of the issues raised by the Foreign Employees' Association appears to be broader than the association's representatives can immediately perceive. This is not only a matter of protecting the interests of foreign employees from any fundamental reform of the Public Works Department's existing organizational law or of issues that directly affect them, but also a matter of how the measures adopted to allow service in the Public Works Department to have a permanent basis should be thoroughly implemented to achieve logical results, thereby helping to establish a sound civil service system. The most valuable legacy that the current International Settlement authorities can hope to pass on to their ultimate successors may be such a system.

E. The Value of a Civil Service System

19. To understand the value of such a legacy in maintaining a high level of financial integrity and establishing sufficient safeguards against bribery and corruption, one only needs to recall the opinions of Mr. Song Ziwen, the Minister of Finance, who stated that "the only true and lasting remedy for eradicating the bad habits and real malpractices of government officials that have existed for centuries" is to establish an effective civil service system. But what is the value of this system to an organization such as the Public Works Department of the International Settlement, or any other organization composed of elected officials that may eventually inherit the responsibilities of the Public Works Department (Note 7)? There are other perspectives that I would like to discuss.

20. Any employer who wants good service from its personnel must establish conditions that enable it to attract suitable people to serve, and must have sufficient guarantees that these conditions will be strictly observed. However, a public organization that has been granted broad governing powers and is composed of people elected through regular public elections is in a very special position. This position makes its ability as an employer fundamentally different from that of individual employers who run their familiar industrial and commercial businesses with individual capabilities, to the point that it cannot be controlled by the power of one person. Compared to other employers, public organizations are generally more completely dependent on the character and abilities of their personnel. These other employers include large industrial and commercial companies whose service organizations are modeled after the civil service system to some extent. The reason why public organizations are so heavily dependent on their personnel is partly due to the nature, scope, and complexity of the work they undertake, but largely due to the method of electing the personnel of these organizations and the fact that their terms of office are generally shorter. Any public organization composed of elected officials must have frequent changes in its members, and people with no experience in handling public affairs may be elected at any time. Such organizations cannot expect to maintain a high level of administration and established customs except by utilizing their officials and employees, who are qualified to preserve this level and these customs. Therefore, whether it is to adapt to changing circumstances or to implement the opinions of the electors and their representatives, it can still guarantee the consistency and continuity of administration when policies need to be changed.

21. In order for the officials of public organizations organized through elections to effectively carry out the important duties they should perform according to the situation, they must enjoy reasonable security of tenure. This security not only gives them the opportunity to gain the necessary experience, but also gives them a certain degree of independence. Government and municipal officials inevitably encounter conflicts with public sentiment or powerful private interests in the performance of their administrative or advisory duties. However, the public interest requires that officials, for the benefit of society as a whole, freely exercise their independent judgment without any reason to fear that they may lose their jobs or that their terms of service will be changed to their detriment as a form of punishment.

22. Any public organization established through elections, such as the Public Works Department of the International Settlement, relies heavily on a large number of capable officials and employees to fulfill its various tasks as a governing body. The terms of their employment should be such that their positions are adequately secured and that they are encouraged to dedicate most of their most productive years to serving the Public Works Department. Therefore, the proper establishment and strict adherence to regulations regarding the security of tenure, remuneration, and training of service personnel is fundamentally important.

23. Therefore, the protection needed by the officials and employees of the Public Works Department, whether it is a special contingency measure created by a fundamental reform of the department's organizational law or part of a permanent system, is not only a protection for the interests of a class of directly related employees, but also a necessary protection for the interests of the Public Works Department as an employer and the society it represents. Both aspects of this issue should be remembered at all times.

24. If any fundamental reform is implemented in the organizational law of the governing body of the International Settlement, regardless of whether the actual result of this reform is consistent with the meaning of the term "recovery" that I have used (Note 8), a provision must be established for the sake of good governance and the interests of both Chinese and foreign employees directly involved. On the one hand, it should guarantee that employees who are dismissed or who wish to resign due to changes in their terms of service can receive fair treatment. On the other hand, it should also allow a large number of personnel with experience under the old system to continue to serve. If the new organization can have these people as advisors and assistants, the risk of disruption or any serious interruption of affairs can be greatly reduced, and the valuable characteristics of the old governance, which have been proven and whose beneficial results have been generally praised, can have a better chance of being maintained under the new circumstances.

F. Three Ways to Solve the Problem

25. I believe that there are three possible ways to achieve all or part of all objectives, that is, to provide more effective security for the terms of service of certain officials and employees of certain parts of the Public Works Department, and thus to make the basis of their service comparable to the basis of a permanent civil service system. The three ways are as follows:

(1) Amendment of the Land Regulations

(2) Resolution of the Ratepayers' Meeting

(3) Modification of the Pension Regulations

I now request that these three methods be briefly described in order. (To be continued)

Science

Tung Oil 229

— Sheng Yanneng

Tung oil is produced in large quantities in our country, but we do not know how to refine and utilize it ourselves, which is a great pity. Fellow countrymen, may you not dismiss this important issue with just the word "pity." We should earnestly study and practically improve it. This is the way to revitalize industry!

On October 26th, this publication published an article by Mr. Nai Zheng titled "Tung Oil Worth Noting," which is very valuable and worth paying attention to. Mr. Nai Zheng spoke in detail about the origin and source of tung oil, but did not mention the aspects of manufacturing (different from method) and inspection, and I also feel that there is a need to supplement the uses of tung oil.

Tung oil is a very important coating, very suitable for the decoration of houses. When applied to wood or ironware, it can prevent the decay of wood and the rusting of ironware. It can also be used as a raw material for white porcelain glaze, floor oil, water-resistant oil, brushing oil, protective film oil, wall painting oil, and various other daily necessities. Now, its properties, manufacturing, uses, and inspection are introduced as follows:

(1) Properties: The film formed by raw tung oil lacks elasticity and does not form a uniform film. Therefore, refined cooked tung oil must be used to be applicable. The characteristic of tung oil is that it can solidify above 500 degrees Fahrenheit and is insoluble in thinners. However, if it is mixed with other oils, its solidification point is often lowered.

(2) Manufacturing: There are many manufacturing methods for tung oil. The following are the manufacturing methods of China, the United States, and Germany:

A. Chinese manufacturing method: Add two qian of litharge and massicot to ten jin of raw tung oil, boil it in a pot, and stir it constantly with a wooden stick. When it boils four or five times, it can be poured into a earthenware bowl and stirred constantly until it cools. (The heat should be moderate, not too strong or too slow, to prevent the tung oil from being too old or too young. The added litharge and massicot are used to make it easy to dry and brighten, and have no other effect.)

B. American manufacturing method: Take ten gallons of raw tung oil, place it in a pot, and heat it slowly to 350 degrees Fahrenheit. Add ten pounds of lead manganese soap. After it is completely dissolved, add five gallons of pure linseed oil and stir constantly. When the temperature reaches 400 degrees Fahrenheit, maintain it for half an hour, then remove from heat and add two to three gallons of thinner.

C. German manufacturing method: Heat the oil to 216 degrees Celsius and maintain it for one hour, stirring constantly without stopping. After removing from heat, thin it with turpentine.

(3) Uses: Tung oil has a wide range of uses, which are described below:

A. Porcelain glaze: Grind tung oil, rosin, artificial lacquer, and transparent porcelain together to obtain white porcelain glaze, which is suitable for the decoration of houses. If the oil is heavy and the resin is light, it can be used to coat woodware.

B. Protective film oil: Mixed oil made with a small amount of tung oil and a large amount of stearin is called protective film oil. When applied to three-in-one soil, it can fill in the small cracks. At the same time, the tung oil in it oxidizes to form a solid protective film to protect the three-in-one soil, so that it does not have flying debris after being trampled.

C. Water-resistant oil: Tung oil and gelatin can be used to make water-resistant oil. When applied to underwater machinery and pipe joints, it can isolate the contact with water.

D. Wall painting oil: Made from tung oil and rosin, it can be washed with water or rain when applied to walls.

E. Floor oil: Add a little stearin to tung oil to make floor oil. When applied to the floor, it can be washed without peeling off and leaves no traces when trampled. It is most suitable for trains and ships.

F. Brushing oil: Also known as baking oil. Used to brush automobile hoods and heaters, it can make them last longer. It is made by boiling tung oil, soybean oil, and a small amount of stearin together to 520 degrees Fahrenheit.

(4) Inspection: To inspect the quality of tung oil, 100 grams of the sample can be placed in a gold pot and heated to 540 degrees Fahrenheit. Pure oil will solidify into a light-colored solid. When cut with a knife, it is not sticky. If the color of the oil is darker and sticky, it is a sign of adulteration.

Society for the Improvement of Social Customs

Points for Improvement Regarding Banquets 230

— Zhu Yunzong

When people encounter events such as marrying a wife, marrying a daughter, sending off friends, or welcoming guests, they always hold banquets for relatives and friends to enjoy themselves. This is enough to connect feelings, and is not to be criticized. However, ordinary banquets nowadays have several shortcomings that must be urgently reformed, which are described in detail below:

(1) The invitation does not specify the time to be seated: Some invitations only state "noon" or "dusk" to be seated, and do not specify the time. However, each time period contains two hours. As a result, guests arrive at different times, and those who arrive early have to wait for those who arrive late, inevitably wasting time!

(2) Giving way: After the host is seated, guests should be seated in order. However, we often see humble people avoiding seats and not sitting down. From this, you push and I respect, making noise and commotion, which is really unnecessary!

(3) Urging people to drink: Alcohol is a stimulating substance, and it is best not to drink it. However, at ordinary banquets, the host often forces people to drink, showing enthusiasm, and harming people in the name of loving them, which I find very puzzling!

(4) Guessing fingers: When the alcohol is high, the host often guesses fingers to enjoy themselves. The phrases "Three Stars," "Four Joys," "First Rank," and "Five Kui" are not only vulgar and unbearable, but also the shouting and noise interfere with public morality. Moreover, it often leads to excessive drinking and loss of life, so what is the joy in doing this!

(5) Too many dishes: Recently, luxury has become fashionable. Whenever there is a banquet, rare delicacies are gathered and precious flavors are displayed. Eaters have limited stomachs and cannot taste all the delicacies, wasting the host's money in vain. Isn't this a miscalculation? Moreover, "the wine of a rich family is enough for a poor man's food for half a year!" and "behind vermilion gates meat and wine go to waste, while on the road lie the bones of those who have frozen to death!" If we only indulge in personal appetites, can we not feel guilty in our hearts when we ask ourselves!

The above, will those who are wise think it is so?

School Scene

All Kinds of Things on the Blackboard 231

— Xiu

Before I rush to talk about it, we are a co-educational school, so before class every day, all kinds of words are written on the blackboard, mostly related to insulting female classmates. It seems that it is especially harsh for Miss × because she is relatively the most flirtatious.

One afternoon, before the first class, the blackboard read "××× (her name) Western painting, ×××, Ding Guagua, don't be smug, a pistol will deal with you,"

Before long, the class bell rang, and the female students all came in together. Seeing many male students laughing and shouting at the blackboard, the female student also gently raised her head, saw her own name written on the blackboard, and showed an unhappy expression on her face. She quickly turned around and reported to the Discipline Office. She happened to meet the Dean of Studies at the door (coming to give a lecture on the issue of seats). The female student then sued the Dean of Studies, and entered the classroom with the Dean of Studies. When the Dean of Studies saw it, he was also very unhappy, slowly wiped off these words, gave a big lecture, and questioned the male students, saying that male students were the same as ordinary things, nothing rare. Besides, you are the highest year in secondary school, and you should not have this kind of unconscious behavior. The students knew that they were wrong, so they sincerely accepted the teachings.

Later, Mr. Qian, a well-known Chinese teacher who studied the psychology of male and female students, gave a profound lecture (the first class was Chinese). All the students applauded. Mr. Qian said: Our human love of the opposite sex is something that cannot be suppressed, and it is something that everyone should have a heart of love, but so-called love must be pure love, true love, and this word of love must be stored in the heart, and cannot be expressed by writing on the blackboard. This is an insulting love, a rupture of love, and the result is the failure of the purpose of seeking love. We must know that love is pure, and when seeking love from a woman, those who love each other love each other, and those who do not love each other do not have to seek love from her again, but instead make her disgusted. At the same time, since we have obtained love, we must not only love her with my love, but also respect her. Respecting her is to abide by etiquette, and respecting and loving are equally important, which is pure love, noble love. On the contrary, it is the love of beasts, the love of barbarians. The ancients said, "Respect and love, then fear." I hope all students will remember this firmly.

In this way, time felt very fast, and the end-of-class bell rang. The female student certainly did not want to let the matter go, and asked the Discipline Office to investigate. This is not to say that the female student is ruthless, but it is a matter that should be investigated.

The second class started, and the school worker took a note from the Discipline Office and called the class monitor and deputy class monitor to ask questions. Later, he called a few more students, but in the end he could not find out. There was nothing that could be done, so he posted a notice saying "Anyone who scribbles on the blackboard again and insults the reputation of others will be severely punished once found out."
